Mortgagee's Right to Demand Debt and Imprison Debtor
States a basic ruling with its rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mortgagee's right to demand the debt and identify the condition under which the judge may imprison the debtor.

Core Idea
A pawn does not block the mortgagee's right to demand the debt—imprisonment is for unjust delay.

This lesson examines a straightforward ruling from al-Quduri's matn: a mortgagee (creditor holding a pawn) may demand repayment of the debt directly from the pawner, even while the pawn remains in his possession. Moreover, if the pawner delays payment without excuse, the judge can imprison him. The passage clarifies that the pawn merely provides additional security—it does not replace the debtor's obligation to pay on time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rights granted to the mortgagee
The passage states two separate rights: (1) the right to demand the debt (al-mutalabah) and (2) the right to have the debtor imprisoned (al-habs) if he delays without excuse.
Both rights are conditional on the debtor being able to pay but refusing.
2
Understand the rationale for the first right
The pawn does not extinguish the debt; it only provides enhanced security (ziyadat al-siyanah). Therefore, the mortgagee's original claim to the debt remains intact. He can demand payment without first selling the pawn.
This counters a potential misconception that the pawn replaces the right to demand.
3
Understand the rationale for imprisonment
Imprisonment is a punishment (jaza') for the debtor's injustice (zulm) in delaying payment (matal). The judge orders it only after the debtor's wrongful delay is established.
Imprisonment is not automatic; judicial determination is required.
4
Note the role of the judge
The judge is the authority who decides whether the debtor is delaying unjustly. Only then does the judge order imprisonment, as detailed in other sections.
The passage refers to 'as we explained in detail previously'—this is a foundational summary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وللمرتهن ان يطالب الراهن بدينه ويحبسه به لان حقه باق بعد الرهن والرهن لزيادة الصيانة فلا تمتنع به المطالبة والحبس جزاء الظلم فاذا ظهر مطله عند القاضي يحبسه كما بيناه على التفصيل فيما تقدم
He (al-Quduri) said: And the mortgagee has the right to demand from the pawner his debt and to imprison him for it, because his right remains after the pawn, and the pawn is for increased protection, so the demand is not prevented by it. And imprisonment is a punishment for injustice. So when his delay becomes apparent before the judge, the judge imprisons him, as we explained in detail previously.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's matn states a basic ruling: the mortgagee can demand repayment of the debt and, if the debtor is able but delays, can have him imprisoned. The reason is that the pawn does not extinguish the debt; it only serves as a security. The mortgagee's right to the debt remains, and the pawn does not hinder the demand. Imprisonment is a punishment for the debtor's wrongdoing (tamattul) in delaying payment. The judge will imprison the debtor only after establishing that he is delaying unfairly. This ruling is standard in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
المطالبة (al-mutalabah): The mortgagee's demand for repayment of the debt from the pawner.
الحبس (al-habs): Imprisonment of the debtor by the judge for delaying payment of a due debt.
الرهن (al-rahn): The pledge or pawn given as security for a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The pawn is lost.
B) The mortgagee demands it immediately after the pawn is given.
C) The pawner's delay becomes apparent to the judge (matal).
D) The pawner has no money at all.

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee can demand the debt directly and, with the judge's order, have the debtor imprisoned for unjust delay—the pawn does not impede this right.

Ruling on Producing the Pawn Before Payment
Ruling on producing the pawn when debt is demanded

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a mortgagee must produce the pawn when demanding the debt, and explain the reason ('illa) of preventing double recovery.

Core Idea
A mortgagee must produce the pawn before receiving payment to avoid double recovery.

This passage addresses a common question in mortgage (rahn) transactions: what must the mortgagee do when he wants to collect the debt? The ruling clarifies that he must first produce the pawn (i.e., bring it to the pawner or court) before receiving payment. The reason behind this is a careful legal reasoning (ta'lil) based on the principle of preventing double recovery.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the mortgagee demanding his debt. The ruling is that he is ordered to produce the pawn. This establishes the obligation.
The verb 'يؤمر' indicates a command, making the ruling wajib.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The evidence is qiyas (legal analogy) based on the concept of qabd al-istifa' (possession for recovery). This concept is key to understanding the reasoning.
The passage explicitly says 'لأن قبض الرهن قبض استيفاء' – because possession of the pawn is possession for recovery.
3
Trace the 'illa (effective cause)
The 'illa is the possibility of double recovery. If the mortgagee receives payment while still holding the pawn, then if the pawn is destroyed in his hands, he would have recovered the debt twice: once through payment and once through the pawn's value. The law prevents this.
'يتكرر الاستيفاء' means double recovery; the possibility of destruction ('على احتمال الهلاك') triggers the prohibition.
4
Apply the principle to a new scenario
Consider a mortgagee who demands payment and receives it without producing the pawn. Later, the pawn is accidentally destroyed. The mortgagee would have both payment and the pawn's value – double recovery. Therefore, production before payment is necessary to avoid this.
This application shows the practical consequence of the 'illa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا طلب المرتهن دينه يؤمر باحضار الرهن لان قبض الرهن قبض استيفاء فلا يجوز ان يقبض ماله مع قيام يد الاستيفاء لانه يتكر را لاستيفاء على اعتبار الهلاك في يد المرتهن وهو محتمل
And when the mortgagee demands his debt, he is ordered to produce the pawn, because possession of the pawn is possession for recovery, so it is not permissible for him to receive his money while the hand of recovery remains, because recovery would be repeated due to considering destruction in the mortgagee's hand, and destruction is possible.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This ruling explains a procedural point: if the mortgagee demands repayment of the debt from the pawner, the mortgagee is required to produce the pawn (i.e., bring it to court or relinquish possession). The reason is that the mortgagee's possession of the pawn is a 'qabd al-istifa'' (recovery possession). If he were to receive the debt payment while still holding the pawn, it would constitute double recovery in case the pawn is later destroyed. The recovery of the debt via payment and the recovery via possession would overlap, and if the pawn is destroyed in his hands, he would have both the debt and the pawn value. To avoid this, he must first produce the pawn, effectively ending his recovery possession, before receiving the payment. This is a safeguard against potential double recovery.

Key Terms
قبض الاستيفاء (qabd al-istifa'): Possession that is considered as recovery of the debt; the mortgagee's possession of the pawn serves as a means to recover the debt if the pawn is destroyed.
يتكرر الاستيفاء (yatakrarr al-istifa'): Double recovery; recovering the debt both through payment and through possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why must the mortgagee produce the pawn when he demands the debt?
A) To prove the existence of the pawn.
B) Because holding the pawn and receiving payment would cause double recovery if the pawn is destroyed.
C) Because the pawner needs to inspect it.
D) Because the judge requires it for documentation.

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee must produce the pawn before receiving the debt because holding the pawn is already a form of recovery; receiving payment with possession would risk double recovery.

Mortgagee's Right to Demand Debt and Imprisonment for Procrastination
Ruling on mortgagee's rights and imprisonment for procrastination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mortgagee's right to demand the debt and the judge's authority to imprison the procrastinating debtor, and explain the legal reasoning based on the pledge's security nature.

Core Idea
A pledge secures the debt, but does not extinguish it—the mortgagee retains the right to demand payment.

This lesson examines a key ruling from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar regarding the rights of a mortgagee. You will learn that taking a pledge does not discharge the debt; rather, the mortgagee may still demand payment. If the debtor deliberately delays, the judge may imprison him as a penalty for oppression. Understanding this ruling clarifies the purpose of a pledge in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Focus on the mortgagee's demand for the debt and the judge's imprisonment of the debtor. The ruling: both are permissible (mubah) under specific conditions.
The mortgagee has the right to demand; the judge has the authority to imprison upon proof of procrastination.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is the legal reasoning (talil) in the text: the mortgagee's right remains after the pledge because the pledge is for additional security (ziyadat al-siyanah), not as a discharge of the debt.
No explicit Quran or hadith is cited; the dalil is the rational implication of the pledge's purpose.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The reasoning: since the pledge does not extinguish the right, demanding payment is still valid. Procrastination (matal) is a form of oppression (zulm), and imprisonment is just punishment for oppression.
The judge must first establish that the debtor is delaying without valid reason.
4
Note the practical implementation
The judge does not imprison automatically; he must verify procrastination. This ruling is part of a broader discussion in Kitab al-Qada (Book of Judgments) in al-Hidayah.
The passage references earlier detailed explanation, indicating consistency in Hanafi law.

Source Text

Commentary: The right of the mortgagee is not discharged by the pledge; rather, the pledge is only so that the mortgagee's money remains secure. So, when this is the case, despite the pledge, the mortgagee has the right to demand his debt from the mortgagor, and if he does not pay, to have him arrested. Since when he does not pay the debt and does not sell the pledged property to pay the debt, the oppression of the mortgagor is established, and imprisonment is the punishment for oppression. The detailed explanation of this has passed in the book of Judgments, chapter on Imprisonment in Hidaya volume 3.

This passage is a ruling from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, conveying that the mortgagee's right to the debt persists even after the pledge is taken. Therefore, the mortgagee may demand payment and, if the mortgagor procrastinates, the judge can imprison him as a punishment for oppression. The commentator expands by clarifying that the pledge does not discharge the debt; it only protects the mortgagee's interest. The debtor's refusal to pay or sell the pledge constitutes oppression, justifying imprisonment. The reference to earlier detailed discussion in Hidaya (Kitab al-Qada) is noted.

Key Terms
حبس (habs): Imprisonment as a judicial punishment for delaying payment when able to pay.
مطل (matal): Procrastination; willful delay in paying a debt despite ability to pay.

Key Takeaway
A pledge (rahn) in Hanafi law secures the debt but does not extinguish it; the mortgagee retains full rights to demand payment and the judge may imprison a procrastinating debtor as a punishment for oppression.

The Mortgagee Must Produce the Pledge When Demanding the Debt
Ruling with proof that the mortgagee must produce the pledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the mortgagee must produce the pledge when demanding the debt and explain the underlying rationale of preventing double recovery.

Core Idea
Possession of a pledge is for security, not ownership; demanding debt while holding it risks double recovery, so the pledge must be produced first.

This lesson examines a crucial procedural ruling in Hanafi mortgage (rahn) law: when the creditor (mortgagee) demands repayment, he must first produce the collateral. The reason lies in the nature of the mortgagee's possession, which is a trust for recovery (qabd istifa). We will explore the ruling, its proof, and the mischief it prevents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Locate the obligated act: the mortgagee is ordered to produce the pledge when demanding the debt. Determine the hukm level from the text's tone (imperative 'yu'maru').
The imperative indicates obligation (wajib) in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Understand the legal rationale (talil)
The text provides the reason: qabd istifa (possessory right for recovery) means the mortgagee holds the pledge solely to secure the debt. Allowing him to collect the debt while still holding the pledge could lead to double recovery if the pledge is later destroyed.
The rationale is a protective measure (sadd al-dhara'i) to prevent harm.
3
Recognize the Hanafi position and its weight
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position from Zahir al-Riwayah. Some later scholars considered it recommended, but the text rules it as ordered (wajib).
The ruling is based on the definition of qabd istifa and the principle of avoiding double recovery.
4
Apply to a modern scenario
Consider a contemporary mortgage: if the bank demands repayment, it must first produce the collateral (e.g., car title). If it collects without producing and the collateral is lost, the debtor suffers double loss.
This ruling protects the debtor's interest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا طلب المرتهن دينه يؤمر باحضار الرهن لان قبض الرهن قبض استيفاء فلا يجوز ان يقبض ماله مع قيام يد الاستيفاء لانه يتكررا لاستيفاء على اعتبار الهلاك في يد المرتهن وهو محتمل
ترجمہ اور جب مرتہن نے اپنے قرض کا مطالبہ کیا تو مرتہن کو مرہون کو حاضر کرنے کا حکم دیا جائے گا اس لئے کہ رہن کا قبضہ وصولیابی کا قبضہ ہوتا ہے تو یہ جائز نہیں کہ مرتہن اپنے قرض پر قبضہ کرے وصولیابی کے قبضہ کے قائم رہنے کے ساتھ ساتھ اس لئے کہ وصولیابی مکرر ہو جائے گی مرتہن کے قبضہ میں ہلاکت کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اور ہلاکت محتمل ہے۔
تشریح مرتہن کے قبضہ میں رہتے ہوئے احتمال ہے کہ مرہون ہلاک ہو جائے اور اس کے باوجود بھی اگر اس کو قرض دیدیا جائے گا تو ذبل وصول ہو جائے گا اس لئے یہ صورت اختیار کی گئی کہ جب مرتین راہن سے اپنا قرض مانگے تو مرتہن سے کہا جائے گا کہ پہلے مرہون کو حاضر کرے۔
And when the mortgagee demands his debt, he is ordered to bring the pledged property, because the possession of the pledge is a possessory right (qabd istifa), so it is not permissible for him to take possession of his money (the debt) while the possessory hand remains in place, because it would result in double recovery, considering the possibility of destruction in the hand of the mortgagee, and destruction is probable. Translation: And when the mortgagee demanded his debt, the mortgagee is ordered to produce the pledge, because the possession of the pledge is a possessory right for recovery. So it is not permissible for the mortgagee to take possession of his debt while the possessory hand remains, because recovery would be repeated, considering the possibility of destruction in the hand of the mortgagee, and destruction is probable. Commentary: While the pledge is in the mortgagee's possession, there is a possibility that it may be destroyed, and if despite that he is given the debt, then it would lead to double recovery. Therefore, it is ruled that when the mortgagee demands his debt from the mortgagor, the mortgagee will be told to first produce the pledge.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling: when the mortgagee demands repayment of the debt, he must first produce the pledged property before the court or the debtor. The reason is that the mortgagee holds the pledge as security (qabd istifa), and if he were allowed to collect the debt while still holding the pledge, it could lead to double recovery if the pledge is later destroyed. The possibility of loss (halaak) makes this precaution necessary. The commentator explains that the mortgagee might receive the debt and then the pledge could be destroyed, resulting in the debtor losing both the property and the money. To prevent this, the pledge must be presented first.

Key Terms
قبض استيفاء (qabd istifa): Possession of the pledge as a means to recover the debt, not as ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why must the mortgagee produce the pledge before demanding the debt?
A) To prove the pledge is still intact.
B) To avoid double recovery if the pledge is later destroyed.
C) To allow the debtor to inspect the pledge.
D) To transfer ownership of the pledge.

Key Takeaway
A mortgagee must produce the pledged property when demanding the debt to prevent double recovery.

Debtor Must Pay Before Pledge Is Returned
Ruling with qiyas analogy to sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that the debtor must pay the debt before the mortgagee returns the pledge, and justify it using qiyas to the sale of a specific item.

Core Idea
Payment precedes release of pledge to ensure equality of rights.

When a mortgagee produces the pledged item, should the debtor pay the debt first or can he reclaim the pledge immediately? The Hanafi school rules that payment must come first, analogizing this to a sale where the buyer pays the price before taking delivery of a specific good. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and parties
State the ruling: when the mortgagee produces the pledge, the debtor is ordered to pay the debt first. Identify the two parties: mortgagee (creditor) and mortgagor (debtor).
2
Understand the rationale: equality of rights
The pledge is a specific item; the debt is unspecified. To equalize their rights, the debt must be paid first, making the creditor's right specified just as the debtor's right in the pledge is specified.
The Arabic text uses 'li-yata'ayyana haqqahu' (so that his right becomes specified).
3
Analyze the qiyas
Identify the asl (sale of a specific item) and its ruling (price paid before delivery). The illa (effective cause) is the need to specify rights and avoid harm. The far' (pledge case) shares this illa, so the same ruling applies.
Asl: مبيع و ثمن; ruling: price given first. Far': رهن; illa: specification of right.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Take a concrete example: a man pledges his car to a bank for a loan. The bank produces the car. Apply the ruling: the debtor must pay the outstanding loan before taking possession of the car.
5
Note the cross-madhhab disagreement
The passage indicates the ruling is mukhtalaf fih (disputed). Some schools may require simultaneous exchange. Recognize that the Hanafi position is based on qiyas, but other valid interpretations exist.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (disagreement) among schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا احضره امر الراهن بتسليم الدين اولا ليتعين حقه كما تعين حق الراهن تحقيقا للتسوية كمافي تسليم المبيع والثمن يحضر المبيع ثم يسلم الثمن اولا
ترجمہ اور جب مرتہن نے رہن کو حاضر کر دیا تو راہن کو اولاً قرض سپرد کرنے کا حکم دیا جائے گا تا کہ مرتین کا حق متعین ہو جائے ، جیسا کہ راہن کا حق متعین ہو گیا برابری کو ثابت کرنے کے لئے جیسا کہ مبیع اور شمن کے سپرد کرنے میں مبیع کو حاضر کیا جاتا ہے پھر پہلے شمن کو سپرد کیا جاتا ہے۔
تشریح جب مرتهن مرہون کو حاضر کر دے تو چونکہ مرہون تو متعین چیز ہے جس میں راہن کا حق متعین ہے اور روپوں میں حق متعین نہیں ہے چونکہ وہ غیر معین ہیں اس لئے برابری کی غرض سے پہلے راہن اس کا قرض ادا کرے پھر مرتہن اس کے درالہ مرہون کو کریگا جیسا کہ مبیع اور شمن میں بھی یہی حکم ہے کہ پہلے شمن دیا جاتا ہے اس کے بعد مبیع حوالہ کیا جائیگا۔
And when he (the mortgagee) produces it, the mortgagor is ordered to deliver the debt first, so that his right becomes specified, just as the right of the mortgagor became specified, to achieve equality, as in the delivery of the sold item and the price: the sold item is produced, then the price is delivered first. Translation: And when the mortgagee has produced the pledge, the mortgagor is ordered to first hand over the debt, so that the mortgagee's right becomes specified, just as the mortgagor's right became specified, to establish equality, as in the delivery of the sold item and the price: the sold item is produced, then the price is handed over first. Commentary: When the mortgagee produces the pledge, since the pledge is a specific thing in which the mortgagor's right is specified, and the money is unspecified, therefore for the sake of equality, the mortgagor should first pay his debt, then the mortgagee will hand over the pledge. Similarly, in sale, the price is given first, then the item is delivered.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This ruling follows the previous: once the pledge is produced, the debtor must pay the debt first before the mortgagee returns the pledge. The reason is that the pledge is a specific item (already identified and in the mortgagee's possession), while the money is not specified. To balance the rights of both parties, payment is made first. The commentator analogizes to a sale where the buyer pays the price before taking delivery of the goods. This ensures that the mortgagee's claim is satisfied before he gives up his security.

Key Terms
مبيع و ثمن (mabi' wa thaman): Sold item and price; analogy used to show order of delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
The qiyas in the passage compares the pledge case to which scenario?
A) A lease contract where rent is paid before use.
B) A sale of a specific item where the price is paid before delivery.
C) A loan where the principal is repaid before collateral is released.
D) A gift where delivery precedes acceptance.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a pledge is produced by the mortgagee, the debtor must pay the debt first to balance the rights of both parties, analogized to a sale where the price precedes delivery.

Demanding Debt in a Different City: Pledge with No Carriage
Ruling on producing the pledge when demanding debt in a different city depending on transport burden

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on producing a pledge when the debt is demanded in a different city, and apply the distinction based on the burden of transport.

Core Idea
A mortgagee must produce a light pledge in any city, but is not required to transport a heavy pledge—takhliya (vacating) suffices.

When a mortgagee demands his debt in a city different from where the pledge contract was made, the rule is not uniform. The obligation to produce the pledge depends on whether moving it involves burden and expense. This lesson explores the Hanafi position that light items must be produced, while heavy items remain where they are, based on the principle of takhliya and avoiding additional harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contractual scenario
The mortgagee demands the debt in a city other than the one where the pledge contract was concluded. Distinguish the two sub-scenarios based on the nature of the pledge.
2
Classify the pledge as light or heavy
Determine whether the pledged item has 'burden and difficulty' (مؤنة و حمل) in transport. Light items: watch, pen, ring. Heavy items: large quantity of cloth, machinery.
3
Apply the ruling to each category
For light pledges: the mortgagee must produce it (same as if within the city). For heavy pledges: the mortgagee collects the debt without producing the pledge.
4
Understand the legal principle
Delivery (تسلیم) in Hanafi law means takhliya (vacating control), not physical transport. Requiring transport of heavy items causes additional harm, which the mortgagee did not undertake.
The analogy with salam: no need to specify place for light items by consensus.
5
Recognize the proof (dalil)
The ruling is based on consensus (اجماع) on salam contracts where specifying place is unnecessary for light goods, and on the principle that obligation is limited to takhliya to avoid harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان طالبه بالدين في غير البلد الذي وقع العقد فيه ان كان الرهن مما لا حمل له ولا مؤنة فكذلك الجواب لان الاماكن كلها في حق التسليم كمكان واحد فيما ليس له حمل ومؤنة ولهذا لا يشترط بيان مكان الايفاء فيه فى باب السلم بالاجماع و ان كان له حمل و مؤنة يستوفى دينه ولا يكلف احضار الرهن لان هذا نقل والواجب عليه التسليم بمعنى التخلية لا النقل من مكان الى مكان لانه يتضرر به زيادة الضرر و لم يلتزم
ترجمہ اور اگر مرتین نے راہن سے قرض کا مطالبہ کیا اس شہر کے علاوہ میں جس میں عقد واقع ہوا تھا تو اگر رہن ان چیزوں میں سے ہے جس کے لئے بوجھ اور مشقت نہیں ہے تو جواب ایسے ہی ہے ( یعنی پہلے مرتہن کو حکم دیا جائے گا کہ رہن کو حاضر کرے ) اس لئے تمام جگہیں سپرد کرنے کے حق میں ایک ہی جگہ کے مثل ہیں اس چیز میں جس کے لئے بوجھ اور مشقت نہ ہو اور اسی وجہ سے ایسی چیز میں (جس کے لئے بوجھ وغیرہ نہ ہو ) بالاجماع باب سلم میں دینے کی جگہ بیان کرنا شرط نہیں ہے اور اگر اس کے لئے بوجھ اور مشقت ہو تو مرتہن اپنا قرض وصول کرے گا اور مرتہی بہن کو حاضر کرنے کا مکلف نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ یہ احضار (رہن) نقل ہے اور مرتہن کے اوپر جو واجب ہے وہ تسلیم ہے جو تخلیہ کے معنی میں ہے نہ کہ ایک جگہ سے دوسری جگہ نقل کرنا اس لئے کہ اس سے مرتہبن زیادہ ضرر اٹھائے گا حالانکہ اس نے ضرر اٹھانے کا التزام نہیں کیا ہے۔
تشریح عقد راہن واقع ہوا تھا مثلاً دیو بند میں اور مرتبہن نے راہن سے اپنے قرض کا مطالبہ کیا دھلی میں تو مرتہن کو مطالبہ کا تو حق ہے لیکن کیا یہاں بھی مرتہن کو حکم دیا جائے گا کہ پہلے مرہون کو حاضر کرے تو فرمایا کہ پہلے یہ دیکھا جائے کہ مرہون کیسی چیز ہے اس کو اٹھانے اور لے جانے میں مشقت ہو گی یا نہیں نیز اس کو لے جانے کے لئے کسی سواری کو طے کرنا پڑیگا یا بغیر اس کے ہی نقل کی جاسکتی ہے اول کی مثال ، گھڑی ، قلم ، انگوٹھی وغیرہ اور ثانی کی مثال، بہت ساری کتا نہیں یا اس کے مثل تو
And if he demands the debt in a city other than the one in which the contract took place, if the pledge is of the type that has no burden or difficulty, then the answer is the same (i.e., the mortgagee is ordered to produce the pledge), because all places are like one place regarding delivery for something that has no burden or difficulty. For this reason, it is not required to specify the place of payment in salam by consensus. And if it has burden and difficulty, he collects his debt and is not obligated to produce the pledge, because this is transportation, and what is obligatory on him is delivery in the sense of vacating (takhliya), not transportation from one place to another, because he would suffer additional harm, and he did not undertake that. Translation: And if the mortgagee demanded the debt in a city other than the one in which the contract took place, if the pledge is from those things for which there is no burden and inconvenience, then the answer is the same (i.e., first the mortgagee will be ordered to produce the pledge), because all places are like one place regarding delivery for something that has no burden and inconvenience. For this reason, it is not a condition to specify the place of payment in salam by consensus. And if it has burden and inconvenience, the mortgagee will collect his debt and will not be obligated to produce the pledge, because this is transportation, and what is obligatory on him is delivery in the sense of vacating, not transportation from one place to another, because he would suffer additional harm, and he did not undertake that. Commentary: The contract of pledge took place, for example, in Deoband, and the mortgagee demanded his debt from the mortgagor in Delhi. So the mortgagee has the right to demand, but will he be ordered here also to first produce the pledge? He said: first it is seen what kind of pledge it is: whether moving it and carrying it will cause difficulty or not, and whether it needs to be transported by a vehicle or can be moved without that. Examples of the first: watch, pen, ring, etc. Examples of the second: a large quantity of cloth or the like.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage deals with the situation where the mortgagee demands the debt in a different city from where the pledge contract was made. The ruling distinguishes based on the nature of the pledge: if it is light and easy to move (like a watch, pen, ring), then the mortgagee must produce it as before, because moving it causes no hardship. In such cases, all places are considered equivalent for delivery, just as in salam contracts where specifying the place is not required. However, if the pledge is heavy and burdensome to transport (like a large quantity of cloth), the mortgagee is not required to produce it; instead, he can simply collect the debt, because delivery (takhliya) is satisfied by relinquishing control, not physically moving the item. Requiring transportation would cause additional harm to the mortgagee, which he did not agree to. The commentator provides examples to clarify the distinction.

Key Terms
تخلیہ (takhliya): Vacating or surrendering control of property, not physically moving it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the pledge is a heavy machine and the mortgagee demands the debt in a different city, what does he do?
A) He must transport the machine to the other city.
B) He collects the debt without producing the machine.
C) He cancels the pledge.
D) He waits until the mortgagor comes to the original city.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the mortgagee's obligation to produce a pledge in a different city depends on the burden of transport: light items must be produced, heavy items are exempt due to the principle of takhliya and avoidance of harm.

The Hanafi Proofs Against Pawning an Undivided Share
Explaining the two proofs and the condition of continuous confinement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi proofs (Quranic verse and qiyas) against pawning musha' and apply the condition of continuous possession to identify invalid pawns.

Core Idea
A pawn requires exclusive continuous possession; an undivided share cannot provide it.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi school's reasoning for the invalidity of pawning an undivided share (musha'). The text presents two key proofs: the Quranic requirement of possession (maqbudatun) and an analogy to an explicit stipulation of alternate possession. Understanding these proofs is essential for correctly applying the ruling in real estate and joint ownership scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two proofs
The text gives a Quranic verse (2:283) and a qiyas (analogy) to a pawner stipulating alternate possession.
2
Analyze the Quranic proof
The verse requires the pawn to be 'maqbudatun' (taken into possession). For a musha', exclusive possession is impossible due to co-ownership.
3
Analyze the qiyas proof
If explicit alternate possession invalidates a pawn, then musha' which inherently involves alternate possession due to co-owner's rights is also invalid.
4
Extract the condition
Both proofs establish that continuous confinement (jabs da'imi) is an essential condition for a valid pawn.
5
Apply to musha'
Since musha' lacks jabs da'imi, pawning it is invalid regardless of divisibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مشاع کا رہن مطلقاً نا جائز ہے
بخلاف الهبة حيث تجوز فيما لا يحتمل القسمة لان المانع فى الهبة غرامة القسمة وهو فيما يقسم اما حكم الهبة الملك والمشاع يقبله وههنا الحكم ثبوت يد الاستيفاء والمشاع لا يقبله وان كان لا يحتمل القسمة

تشریح مشاع کا رہن مطلقا نا جائز ہے خواہ وہ مشاع قابل قسمت ہو یا نہ ہو اس طرح مشاع کا رہن جائز نہیں ہوگا خواہ شیوع ابتداء میں ہو یا بعد میں طاری ہوا ہو (کما سیاتی)
مشاع کے بہہ میں تفصیل ہے اگر مشاع ایسا ہو جو قیم ہوسکتا ہے تو اسکا یہ بھی جائز نہیں ہے اور اگر مشاع ایسا ہو کہ اس کی تقسیم نہیں کی جاسکتی تو ایسے مشاع کا ہیہ جائز ہے۔ پہلی صورت اس لئے جائز نہیں کہ اس میں واہب پر یہ فریضہ عائد ہوگا کہ وہ موہوب لیہ کو موہوب سپر د کر دے اس حال میں کہ اس کا ہوارہ کیا جا چکا ہو لہذا واہب پر قیمت کا تاوان پڑے گا جس کا اس نے التزام نہیں کیا۔ اور دوسری صورت میں ہبہ اس لئے جائز ہو گیا کہ اس میں قسمت کا تاوان واہب پر عائد نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ وہ قیمت کے قابل ہے ہی نہیں جب یہ تفصیل ذہن نشیں ہو گئی تو اب سنئے۔
معترض کہتا ہے کہ جب غیر قابل قسمت کا ہہ جائز ہے تو اس کا رہن بھی جائز ہونا چاہیے؟ تو مصنف نے اس کا جواب دیا کہ یہ قیاس مع الفارق ہے کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ بیبہ کا مقصد اور اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ موہوب لہ اس کا مالک بن جائے اور ملکیت مشاع کے اوپر بھی ثابت ہوتی ہے جیسا کہ غیر مشاع پر ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ اور رہن کا حکم ہی اور ہے اور وہ ید استیفاء کا ثبوت ہے اور یہ حکم مشاع میں حاصل نہ ہو سکے گا خواہ قابل قسمت ہو یا نہ ہو۔
سوال جب بات یوں ہے کہ ہبہ کا حکم ثبوت ملک ہے تو قابل قسمت کا بہ بھی صحیح ہونا چاہیے؟ جواب یہ بھی قیاس مع الفارق ہے کیونکہ قابل قسمت میں واہب قسمت کی مشقت میں پھنسے گا اور غیر قابل قسمت میں یہ بات نہیں
سے "فلا اشکال فیہ"۔
رہمن مشاع کے عدم جواز کی دو دلیلیں
ولا يجوز من شريكه لانه لا يقبل حكمه على الوجه الأول وعلى الوجه الثاني يسكن يوما بحكم الملك ويوما بحكم الرهن فيصير كانه رهن يوما ويوما لا
ترجمہ اور جائز نہیں ہے (مشاع کا رہن) اپنے شریک کے ہاتھ اس لئے کہ یہ دہن مشاع رہن کے حکم کو قبول نہیں کرے گا، وجہ اول کے مطابق اور وجہ ثانی کے مطابق مرتبین اس میں ایک دن رہیگا ملکیت کے اور ایک دن رہن کے حکم سے تو ایسا ہو جائے گا گویا کہ اس نے ایک دن رہن کو رکھا اور ایک دن رہن نہیں رکھا۔ تشریح رہن مشاع کے عدم جواز کی دو دلیلیں ماقبل میں بیان کی گئی ہیں۔
ید استیفاء کا عدم ثبوت
جبس دائمی کا استحقاق اب سنئے اگر کسی نے ایسا گھر رہن رکھا جو اس کے اور زید کے درمیان شیوع کے طریقہ پر مشترک ہے اور زید ہی کے پاس رہن رکھا تو یہ بھی نا جائز ہے کیونکہ دلیل اول کے مطابق حکم رہن ید استیفاء کا ثبوت ہے اور وہ یہاں مفقود ہے کیونکہ مشاع پر ید استیفاء کا ثبوت ہوتا ہی نہیں ہے۔
اور دلیل ثانی کے مطابق بھی رہن جائز نہ ہوگا کیونکہ جس دائگی مفقود ہے بلکہ یہاں تو صورت یہ ہوگی کہ مرتہن اس میں ایک دن تو اپنی ملک کے لحاظ سے رہے گا اور دوسرے دن رہن کے اعتبار سے گویا کہ ایک دن رہن ہے اور دوسرے دن نہیں ہے اور اس کا عدم جواز ماقبل میں مصرح سے لہذا شریک کے ہاتھ ہی مشاع کا رہن جائز نہیں ہے۔
شیوع طاری کا ... اقوال فقہاء
والشيوع الطاري يمنع بقاء الرهن في رواية الأصل وعن ابي يوسف انه لا يمنع لان حكم البقاء اسهل من حكم الابتداء فاشبه الهبة
Book of Rahn. Then perpetual confinement will be lost because here distribution of benefits becomes necessary, so it becomes as if the pawner said: I pawned it for one day and not for the other day. For this reason, pawning is not valid in things that are susceptible to division, and in things that are not susceptible to division. Explanation: This is our second proof. Its gist is that possession of the pawned item is a condition, as indicated by the divine statement {pledges taken into possession} (2:283). Also, the objective of pawning clarifies this because the objective of pawning is to obtain strength so that the pawner cannot deny the debt. In any case, the essence of strength and possession is that the pawned item remains confined with the mortgagee continuously and the mortgagee has the right to retain it until the debt is paid. In an undivided share, continuous confinement is impossible because the right of another exists in it. If pawning an undivided share is considered valid, then allocation (muhayat) becomes necessary: one day it remains with the mortgagee and the next day with the pawner's co-owner. This is invalid just as if the pawner explicitly says about an undivided pawned item: it will be with the mortgagee one day and with me the next day—this is invalid, so the former is also invalid. Since it is established that in an undivided share continuous confinement, which is necessary in pawning, is lost, then pawning an undivided share is invalid whether it is divisible or not because continuous confinement is absent in both cases. Pawning an undivided share is absolutely invalid. Contrary to gift (hibah) which is valid in things not susceptible to division because the impediment in gift is the harm of division, and that is present in what can be divided. As for the ruling of gift, it is ownership, and an undivided share accepts ownership. Here the ruling is the establishment of the hand of collection (yad al-istifa'), and an undivided share does not accept it, even if it is not susceptible to division. Translation: Contrary to gift, in that gift is valid for things that are not divisible, because in gift the impediment is the harm of division, and this (harm of division) will be in what can be divided. In any case, the ruling of gift is ownership, and an undivided share accepts ownership, whereas here (in pawning) the ruling is the establishment of the hand of collection, and an undivided share does not accept it, even if it does not admit division. Explanation: Pawning an undivided share is absolutely invalid, whether that undivided share is divisible or not. Likewise, pawning an undivided share will not be valid whether the common ownership arises initially or later (as will come). There is a difference in pawning an undivided share. If the undivided share is such that it can be divided, then its gift is also not valid. If the undivided share is such that it cannot be divided, then its gift is valid. The first case is invalid because it would require the donor to hand over the gift to the donee after it has been divided, so the donor would incur loss of value which he did not undertake. The second case is valid because the harm of division does not fall upon the donor since it is not subject to value. When this detail is understood, listen now. The objector says: When gift of something not divisible is valid, then its pawning should also be valid. The author replied that this is an analogy with a difference. Why? Because the objective and ruling of gift is that the donee becomes its owner, and ownership is established over an undivided share just as over a non-undivided share. The ruling of pawning is different: it is the establishment of the hand of collection, and this ruling cannot be obtained in an undivided share, whether divisible or not. Question: If the matter is that the ruling of gift is establishment of ownership, then gift of a divisible thing should also be valid? Answer: This too is an analogy with a difference, because in a divisible thing, the donor gets caught in the hardship of division, while in a non-divisible thing, that is not the case, so there is no difficulty. Two proofs for the impermissibility of pawning an undivided share. And it is not valid from his co-owner because it does not accept the ruling in the first manner, and in the second manner, he will live one day by virtue of ownership and one day by virtue of pawning, so it becomes as if he pawned it one day and not the other. Translation: And pawning (an undivided share) from his partner is not valid because this undivided share will not accept the ruling of pawning according to the first reason, and according to the second reason, the mortgagee will stay in it one day by virtue of ownership and one day by virtue of pawning, so it becomes as if he kept the pawn one day and not the other. Explanation: Two proofs for the impermissibility of pawning an undivided share were mentioned previously. Non-establishment of the hand of collection and the requirement of continuous confinement. Now listen: If someone pawns a house that is shared between him and Zaid on the basis of common ownership, and he pawns it with Zaid himself, then this is also invalid because according to the first proof, the ruling of pawning is the establishment of the hand of collection, and that is lacking here because the hand of collection is not established over an undivided share. According to the second proof, pawning will also be invalid because continuous confinement is absent; rather, the situation will be that the mortgagee will stay in it one day by virtue of his own ownership and another day by virtue of pawning, meaning it is a pawn one day and not the other, and its impermissibility is clear from what preceded. Therefore, pawning an undivided share from a partner is not valid. Supervening common ownership... statements of jurists. And supervening common ownership prevents the continuation of the pawn in the original narration, and from Abu Yusuf that it does not prevent, because the rule of continuation is easier than the rule of initiation, so it resembles gift.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the impermissibility of pawning an undivided share (musha') in the Hanafi school. It presents two core proofs: (1) the hand of collection (yad al-istifa') cannot be established over a musha' share, and (2) continuous confinement (jabs da'imi) is impossible because the share is jointly owned and must be rotated. The passage then draws a critical distinction between pawning and gift (hibah). While gift of a musha' that is indivisible is valid (since ownership can be established over a share), pawning of any musha'—whether divisible or not—is invalid because the purpose of pawning is not ownership but the right to retain and collect payment, which requires exclusive and continuous possession. The author also addresses an objection: if gift of an indivisible musha' is valid, why not pawning? The answer is that gift's ruling is ownership (which can be in a share), whereas pawning's ruling is the hand of collection (which cannot be in a share). Finally, the passage discusses the case where the musha' is pawned to a co-owner—it is also invalid for the same reasons. At the end, it mentions a subtle intra-Hanafi difference: if common ownership arises after a valid pawn (shuyu' tari'), the original narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) holds that it invalidates the pawn, while Abu Yusuf says it does not, analogizing to gift since continuation is easier than initiation. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the original narration.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A contract whereby a valuable item is given as security for a debt, to be retained by the creditor until repayment.
مشاع (musha'): An undivided share in a jointly owned property, where each co-owner's share is not physically separated.
ید استیفاء (yad al-istifa'): The hand or right of collection and retention; the right held by the mortgagee to take and keep the pawned item until the debt is paid.
جبس دائمی (jabs da'imi): Continuous and uninterrupted confinement of the pawned item with the mortgagee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is the primary reason pawning an undivided share (musha') is invalid?
A) The pawner does not own the share.
B) The hand of collection (yad al-istifa') cannot be established.
C) The Quran does not mention undivided shares.
D) The mortgagee cannot take possession until division.

Key Takeaway
Pawning an undivided share is invalid because the essential conditions of continuous confinement and the hand of collection cannot be fulfilled.

Distinguishing Pawning from Gift: The Hand of Collection vs Ownership
Distinguishing between pawning and gifting musha', and responding to an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why pawning a musha' is invalid even when gifting the same musha' is valid, and evaluate the objection that uses gift as an analogy.

Core Idea
Gift transfers ownership which can be in a share; pawning requires a possessory right that cannot be shared.

In this lesson, we examine the distinction between pawning and gifting an undivided share (musha'). The text addresses an objection: if gift of an indivisible musha' is valid, why is pawning invalid? The answer lies in the different legal effects: gift establishes ownership (milk), which can be in a share, while pawning establishes the hand of collection (yad al-istifa'), which requires exclusive control. This distinction is crucial for understanding the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
An objector notes that gift of an indivisible musha' is valid, so pawning should also be valid by analogy.
2
Understand the Hanafi distinction
The author distinguishes between the rulings of gift and pawning: gift's ruling is ownership (milk), which can be established over a musha'; pawning's ruling is the hand of collection (yad al-istifa'), which cannot be established over a musha'.
3
Explain why gift of divisible musha' is invalid
Gift of a divisible musha' is invalid because it would impose the harm of division on the donor. For indivisible musha', no such harm exists, so gift is valid.
4
Apply the distinction to pawning
Since pawning requires yad al-istifa', which is incompatible with common ownership, pawning any musha' (divisible or not) is invalid.
5
Answer the objection
The objection is based on a false analogy (qiyas ma'a al-fariq). The difference in legal effects makes pawning and gift fundamentally different.

كتاب الرهن
تو دوام فوت ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ یہاں منافع کی تقسیم ضروری ہوگی تو یہ ایسا ہو جائے گا گویا کہ راہن نے یوں کہا کہ میں نے ایک دن رہن رکھا اور دوسرے دن نہیں رکھا اسی وجہ سے رہن جائز نہیں ہوتا ان چیزوں میں جو قسمت کا احتمال رکھتی ہیں اور ان چیزوں میں جو تقسیم کا احتمال نہیں رکھتیں۔
تشریح یہ ہماری دوسری دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ رہن کا مقبوض ہونا شرط ہے جیسا کہ فرمان باری ﴿فَرِهَـٰنࣱ مَّقۡبُوضَةࣱ﴾ اس پر دال ہے نیز رہن کا مقصود بھی اسی کو واضح کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ رہن کا مقصود یہ ہے کہ مضبوطی حاصل ہو جائے تا کہ راہن قرض کا انکار نہ کر سکے۔
بہر حال مضبوطی اور قبضہ کی اصل کرے کیسے بھری ہے کہ مرہون برابر مرتہن کے پاس محبوس رہے اور مرتہن کو تا اداء دین جس کا استحقاق رہے اور مشاع میں جبس دائمی ہو نہیں سکتا کیونکہ اس میں دوسرے کا حق موجود ہے اگر مشاع کے رہن کو جائز قرار دیا جائے تو اس میں مہایات ضروری ہوگی کہ ایک دن وہ مرتہن کے پاس رہے اور دوسرے دن راہن کے شریک کے پاس رہے اور یہ ایسے ہی نا جائز ہے جیسا کہ اگر راہن غیر مشاع مرہون کے بارے میں صراحتہ یہ کہ دے کہ مرہون ایک دن مرتہن کے پاس رہے گا اور ایک دن میرے پاس اور یہ نا جائز ہے تو اول بھی جائز نہ ہوگا جب یہ بات ہوئی کہ مشاع میں جبس دائمی فوت ہو جائے گا جو رہن میں ضروری ہے تو مشاع کا رہن جائز نہ ہوگا خواہ وہ قابل تقسیم ہو یا قابل تقسیم نہ ہو کیونکہ جبس دائمی دونوں صورتوں میں مفقود ہے۔
مشاع کا رہن مطلقاً نا جائز ہے
بخلاف الهبة حيث تجوز فيما لا يحتمل القسمة لان المانع فى الهبة غرامة القسمة وهو فيما يقسم اما حكم الهبة الملك والمشاع يقبله وههنا الحكم ثبوت يد الاستيفاء والمشاع لا يقبله وان كان لا يحتمل القسمة
ترجمہ بخلاف ہبہ کے اس حیثیت سے کہ ہبہ جائز ہے ان چیزوں کا جو قابل قسمت نہ ہوں اس لئے کہ ہبہ کے اندر مانع بٹوارہ کا ضرر ہے اور یہ (غرامتہ القسمہ) اس چیز میں ہوگا جو تقسیم کی جاسکتی ہے بہر حال بہہ کا حکم ملک ہے اور مشاع ملک کو قبول کرتا ہے اور یہاں (رہن میں حکم ید استیفاء کا ثبوت ہے) اور مشاع اس کو قبول نہیں کرتا اگر چہ وہ تقسیم کا احتمال نہ رکھتا ہو۔
تشریح مشاع کا رہن مطلقا نا جائز ہے خواہ وہ مشاع قابل قسمت ہو یا نہ ہو اس طرح مشاع کا رہن جائز نہیں ہوگا خواہ شیوع ابتداء میں ہو یا بعد میں طاری ہوا ہو (کما سیاتی)
مشاع کے بہہ میں تفصیل ہے اگر مشاع ایسا ہو جو قیم ہوسکتا ہے تو اسکا یہ بھی جائز نہیں ہے اور اگر مشاع ایسا ہو کہ اس کی تقسیم نہیں کی جاسکتی تو ایسے مشاع کا ہیہ جائز ہے۔ پہلی صورت اس لئے جائز نہیں کہ اس میں واہب پر یہ فریضہ عائد ہوگا کہ وہ موہوب لیہ کو موہوب سپر د کر دے اس حال میں کہ اس کا ہوارہ کیا جا چکا ہو لہذا واہب پر قیمت کا تاوان پڑے گا جس کا اس نے التزام نہیں کیا۔ اور دوسری صورت میں ہبہ اس لئے جائز ہو گیا کہ اس میں قسمت کا تاوان واہب پر عائد نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ وہ قیمت کے قابل ہے ہی نہیں جب یہ تفصیل ذہن نشیں ہو گئی تو اب سنئے۔
معترض کہتا ہے کہ جب غیر قابل قسمت کا ہہ جائز ہے تو اس کا رہن بھی جائز ہونا چاہیے؟ تو مصنف نے اس کا جواب دیا کہ یہ قیاس مع الفارق ہے کیوں؟ اس لئے کہ بیبہ کا مقصد اور اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ موہوب لہ اس کا مالک بن جائے اور ملکیت مشاع کے اوپر بھی ثابت ہوتی ہے جیسا کہ غیر مشاع پر ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ اور رہن کا حکم ہی اور ہے اور وہ ید استیفاء کا ثبوت ہے اور یہ حکم مشاع میں حاصل نہ ہو سکے گا خواہ قابل قسمت ہو یا نہ ہو۔
سوال جب بات یوں ہے کہ ہبہ کا حکم ثبوت ملک ہے تو قابل قسمت کا بہ بھی صحیح ہونا چاہیے؟ جواب یہ بھی قیاس مع الفارق ہے کیونکہ قابل قسمت میں واہب قسمت کی مشقت میں پھنسے گا اور غیر قابل قسمت میں یہ بات نہیں
سے "فلا اشکال فیہ"۔
رہمن مشاع کے عدم جواز کی دو دلیلیں
ولا يجوز من شريكه لانه لا يقبل حكمه على الوجه الأول وعلى الوجه الثاني يسكن يوما بحكم الملك ويوما بحكم الرهن فيصير كانه رهن يوما ويوما لا
ترجمہ اور جائز نہیں ہے (مشاع کا رہن) اپنے شریک کے ہاتھ اس لئے کہ یہ دہن مشاع رہن کے حکم کو قبول نہیں کرے گا، وجہ اول کے مطابق اور وجہ ثانی کے مطابق مرتبین اس میں ایک دن رہیگا ملکیت کے اور ایک دن رہن کے حکم سے تو ایسا ہو جائے گا گویا کہ اس نے ایک دن رہن کو رکھا اور ایک دن رہن نہیں رکھا۔ تشریح رہن مشاع کے عدم جواز کی دو دلیلیں ماقبل میں بیان کی گئی ہیں۔
ید استیفاء کا عدم ثبوت
جبس دائمی کا استحقاق اب سنئے اگر کسی نے ایسا گھر رہن رکھا جو اس کے اور زید کے درمیان شیوع کے طریقہ پر مشترک ہے اور زید ہی کے پاس رہن رکھا تو یہ بھی نا جائز ہے کیونکہ دلیل اول کے مطابق حکم رہن ید استیفاء کا ثبوت ہے اور وہ یہاں مفقود ہے کیونکہ مشاع پر ید استیفاء کا ثبوت ہوتا ہی نہیں ہے۔
اور دلیل ثانی کے مطابق بھی رہن جائز نہ ہوگا کیونکہ جس دائگی مفقود ہے بلکہ یہاں تو صورت یہ ہوگی کہ مرتہن اس میں ایک دن تو اپنی ملک کے لحاظ سے رہے گا اور دوسرے دن رہن کے اعتبار سے گویا کہ ایک دن رہن ہے اور دوسرے دن نہیں ہے اور اس کا عدم جواز ماقبل میں مصرح سے لہذا شریک کے ہاتھ ہی مشاع کا رہن جائز نہیں ہے۔
شیوع طاری کا ... اقوال فقہاء
والشيوع الطاري يمنع بقاء الرهن في رواية الأصل وعن ابي يوسف انه لا يمنع لان حكم البقاء اسهل من حكم الابتداء فاشبه الهبة
Book of Rahn. Then perpetual confinement will be lost because here distribution of benefits becomes necessary, so it becomes as if the pawner said: I pawned it for one day and not for the other day. For this reason, pawning is not valid in things that are susceptible to division, and in things that are not susceptible to division. Explanation: This is our second proof. Its gist is that possession of the pawned item is a condition, as indicated by the divine statement {pledges taken into possession} (2:283). Also, the objective of pawning clarifies this because the objective of pawning is to obtain strength so that the pawner cannot deny the debt. In any case, the essence of strength and possession is that the pawned item remains confined with the mortgagee continuously and the mortgagee has the right to retain it until the debt is paid. In an undivided share, continuous confinement is impossible because the right of another exists in it. If pawning an undivided share is considered valid, then allocation (muhayat) becomes necessary: one day it remains with the mortgagee and the next day with the pawner's co-owner. This is invalid just as if the pawner explicitly says about an undivided pawned item: it will be with the mortgagee one day and with me the next day—this is invalid, so the former is also invalid. Since it is established that in an undivided share continuous confinement, which is necessary in pawning, is lost, then pawning an undivided share is invalid whether it is divisible or not because continuous confinement is absent in both cases. Pawning an undivided share is absolutely invalid. Contrary to gift (hibah) which is valid in things not susceptible to division because the impediment in gift is the harm of division, and that is present in what can be divided. As for the ruling of gift, it is ownership, and an undivided share accepts ownership. Here the ruling is the establishment of the hand of collection (yad al-istifa'), and an undivided share does not accept it, even if it is not susceptible to division. Translation: Contrary to gift, in that gift is valid for things that are not divisible, because in gift the impediment is the harm of division, and this (harm of division) will be in what can be divided. In any case, the ruling of gift is ownership, and an undivided share accepts ownership, whereas here (in pawning) the ruling is the establishment of the hand of collection, and an undivided share does not accept it, even if it does not admit division. Explanation: Pawning an undivided share is absolutely invalid, whether that undivided share is divisible or not. Likewise, pawning an undivided share will not be valid whether the common ownership arises initially or later (as will come). There is a difference in pawning an undivided share. If the undivided share is such that it can be divided, then its gift is also not valid. If the undivided share is such that it cannot be divided, then its gift is valid. The first case is invalid because it would require the donor to hand over the gift to the donee after it has been divided, so the donor would incur loss of value which he did not undertake. The second case is valid because the harm of division does not fall upon the donor since it is not subject to value. When this detail is understood, listen now. The objector says: When gift of something not divisible is valid, then its pawning should also be valid. The author replied that this is an analogy with a difference. Why? Because the objective and ruling of gift is that the donee becomes its owner, and ownership is established over an undivided share just as over a non-undivided share. The ruling of pawning is different: it is the establishment of the hand of collection, and this ruling cannot be obtained in an undivided share, whether divisible or not. Question: If the matter is that the ruling of gift is establishment of ownership, then gift of a divisible thing should also be valid? Answer: This too is an analogy with a difference, because in a divisible thing, the donor gets caught in the hardship of division, while in a non-divisible thing, that is not the case, so there is no difficulty. Two proofs for the impermissibility of pawning an undivided share. And it is not valid from his co-owner because it does not accept the ruling in the first manner, and in the second manner, he will live one day by virtue of ownership and one day by virtue of pawning, so it becomes as if he pawned it one day and not the other. Translation: And pawning (an undivided share) from his partner is not valid because this undivided share will not accept the ruling of pawning according to the first reason, and according to the second reason, the mortgagee will stay in it one day by virtue of ownership and one day by virtue of pawning, so it becomes as if he kept the pawn one day and not the other. Explanation: Two proofs for the impermissibility of pawning an undivided share were mentioned previously. Non-establishment of the hand of collection and the requirement of continuous confinement. Now listen: If someone pawns a house that is shared between him and Zaid on the basis of common ownership, and he pawns it with Zaid himself, then this is also invalid because according to the first proof, the ruling of pawning is the establishment of the hand of collection, and that is lacking here because the hand of collection is not established over an undivided share. According to the second proof, pawning will also be invalid because continuous confinement is absent; rather, the situation will be that the mortgagee will stay in it one day by virtue of his own ownership and another day by virtue of pawning, meaning it is a pawn one day and not the other, and its impermissibility is clear from what preceded. Therefore, pawning an undivided share from a partner is not valid. Supervening common ownership... statements of jurists. And supervening common ownership prevents the continuation of the pawn in the original narration, and from Abu Yusuf that it does not prevent, because the rule of continuation is easier than the rule of initiation, so it resembles gift.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the impermissibility of pawning an undivided share (musha') in the Hanafi school. It presents two core proofs: (1) the hand of collection (yad al-istifa') cannot be established over a musha' share, and (2) continuous confinement (jabs da'imi) is impossible because the share is jointly owned and must be rotated. The passage then draws a critical distinction between pawning and gift (hibah). While gift of a musha' that is indivisible is valid (since ownership can be established over a share), pawning of any musha'—whether divisible or not—is invalid because the purpose of pawning is not ownership but the right to retain and collect payment, which requires exclusive and continuous possession. The author also addresses an objection: if gift of an indivisible musha' is valid, why not pawning? The answer is that gift's ruling is ownership (which can be in a share), whereas pawning's ruling is the hand of collection (which cannot be in a share). Finally, the passage discusses the case where the musha' is pawned to a co-owner—it is also invalid for the same reasons. At the end, it mentions a subtle intra-Hanafi difference: if common ownership arises after a valid pawn (shuyu' tari'), the original narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) holds that it invalidates the pawn, while Abu Yusuf says it does not, analogizing to gift since continuation is easier than initiation. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the original narration.

Key Terms
ہبہ (hibah): Gift; a contract transferring ownership of a property without consideration.
ملک (milk): Ownership; the right to possess, use, and dispose of property.
قیاس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): An analogy that is invalid because of a fundamental difference between the two cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is gift of an indivisible undivided share valid but pawning the same share invalid in the Hanafi school?
A) Because gift requires less stringent possession than pawning.
B) Because gift's ruling is ownership, which can be in a share, while pawning's ruling is the hand of collection, which cannot.
C) Because pawning is a form of sale, not gift.
D) Because the Quran allows gift but not pawning of musha'.

Key Takeaway
Pawning and gifting an undivided share are governed by different legal effects: ownership can be shared, but the right to possess exclusively cannot.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Pawning a Musha' to a Co-Owner and Supervening Common Ownership
Extending the ruling to pawning to a co-owner and discussing supervening common ownership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling that pawning a musha' to a co-owner is invalid and distinguish the two positions on supervening common ownership (shuyu' tari').

Core Idea
Even when the mortgagee is the co-owner, pawning a musha' is invalid due to the lack of continuous confinement.

In this lesson, we extend the ruling to two specific scenarios: pawning an undivided share to the co-owner themselves, and the case where common ownership arises after a valid pawn (shuyu' tari'). The text explains that even when the mortgagee is the co-owner, the pawn is invalid because the mortgagee's possession alternates between ownership and pawn rights, breaking continuous confinement. For supervening common ownership, the Hanafi school has an internal difference: the original narration invalidates the pawn, while Abu Yusuf holds it continues by analogy to gift.

Guided Path
1
Understand the co-owner scenario
When a musha' is pawned to a co-owner, the mortgagee already has ownership rights. They will occupy the property one day as owner and one day as mortgagee, breaking continuous confinement.
2
Apply the two proofs
First proof: yad al-istifa' cannot be established over a musha', even when the mortgagee is the co-owner. Second proof: continuous confinement is lost due to alternating possession.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on shuyu' tari'
Supervening common ownership (e.g., inheritance after a valid pawn) is treated differently by Abu Yusuf: he argues that continuation is easier than initiation, so the pawn remains valid.
4
Know the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that shuyu' tari' invalidates the pawn, just like initial common ownership.

سے "فلا اشکال فیہ"۔
رہمن مشاع کے عدم جواز کی دو دلیلیں
ولا يجوز من شريكه لانه لا يقبل حكمه على الوجه الأول وعلى الوجه الثاني يسكن يوما بحكم الملك ويوما بحكم الرهن فيصير كانه رهن يوما ويوما لا
ترجمہ اور جائز نہیں ہے (مشاع کا رہن) اپنے شریک کے ہاتھ اس لئے کہ یہ دہن مشاع رہن کے حکم کو قبول نہیں کرے گا، وجہ اول کے مطابق اور وجہ ثانی کے مطابق مرتبین اس میں ایک دن رہیگا ملکیت کے اور ایک دن رہن کے حکم سے تو ایسا ہو جائے گا گویا کہ اس نے ایک دن رہن کو رکھا اور ایک دن رہن نہیں رکھا۔ تشریح رہن مشاع کے عدم جواز کی دو دلیلیں ماقبل میں بیان کی گئی ہیں۔
ید استیفاء کا عدم ثبوت
جبس دائمی کا استحقاق اب سنئے اگر کسی نے ایسا گھر رہن رکھا جو اس کے اور زید کے درمیان شیوع کے طریقہ پر مشترک ہے اور زید ہی کے پاس رہن رکھا تو یہ بھی نا جائز ہے کیونکہ دلیل اول کے مطابق حکم رہن ید استیفاء کا ثبوت ہے اور وہ یہاں مفقود ہے کیونکہ مشاع پر ید استیفاء کا ثبوت ہوتا ہی نہیں ہے۔
اور دلیل ثانی کے مطابق بھی رہن جائز نہ ہوگا کیونکہ جس دائگی مفقود ہے بلکہ یہاں تو صورت یہ ہوگی کہ مرتہن اس میں ایک دن تو اپنی ملک کے لحاظ سے رہے گا اور دوسرے دن رہن کے اعتبار سے گویا کہ ایک دن رہن ہے اور دوسرے دن نہیں ہے اور اس کا عدم جواز ماقبل میں مصرح سے لہذا شریک کے ہاتھ ہی مشاع کا رہن جائز نہیں ہے۔
شیوع طاری کا ... اقوال فقہاء
والشيوع الطاري يمنع بقاء الرهن في رواية الأصل وعن ابي يوسف انه لا يمنع لان حكم البقاء اسهل من حكم الابتداء فاشبه الهبة
Book of Rahn. Then perpetual confinement will be lost because here distribution of benefits becomes necessary, so it becomes as if the pawner said: I pawned it for one day and not for the other day. For this reason, pawning is not valid in things that are susceptible to division, and in things that are not susceptible to division. Explanation: This is our second proof. Its gist is that possession of the pawned item is a condition, as indicated by the divine statement {pledges taken into possession} (2:283). Also, the objective of pawning clarifies this because the objective of pawning is to obtain strength so that the pawner cannot deny the debt. In any case, the essence of strength and possession is that the pawned item remains confined with the mortgagee continuously and the mortgagee has the right to retain it until the debt is paid. In an undivided share, continuous confinement is impossible because the right of another exists in it. If pawning an undivided share is considered valid, then allocation (muhayat) becomes necessary: one day it remains with the mortgagee and the next day with the pawner's co-owner. This is invalid just as if the pawner explicitly says about an undivided pawned item: it will be with the mortgagee one day and with me the next day—this is invalid, so the former is also invalid. Since it is established that in an undivided share continuous confinement, which is necessary in pawning, is lost, then pawning an undivided share is invalid whether it is divisible or not because continuous confinement is absent in both cases. Pawning an undivided share is absolutely invalid. Contrary to gift (hibah) which is valid in things not susceptible to division because the impediment in gift is the harm of division, and that is present in what can be divided. As for the ruling of gift, it is ownership, and an undivided share accepts ownership. Here the ruling is the establishment of the hand of collection (yad al-istifa'), and an undivided share does not accept it, even if it is not susceptible to division. Translation: Contrary to gift, in that gift is valid for things that are not divisible, because in gift the impediment is the harm of division, and this (harm of division) will be in what can be divided. In any case, the ruling of gift is ownership, and an undivided share accepts ownership, whereas here (in pawning) the ruling is the establishment of the hand of collection, and an undivided share does not accept it, even if it does not admit division. Explanation: Pawning an undivided share is absolutely invalid, whether that undivided share is divisible or not. Likewise, pawning an undivided share will not be valid whether the common ownership arises initially or later (as will come). There is a difference in pawning an undivided share. If the undivided share is such that it can be divided, then its gift is also not valid. If the undivided share is such that it cannot be divided, then its gift is valid. The first case is invalid because it would require the donor to hand over the gift to the donee after it has been divided, so the donor would incur loss of value which he did not undertake. The second case is valid because the harm of division does not fall upon the donor since it is not subject to value. When this detail is understood, listen now. The objector says: When gift of something not divisible is valid, then its pawning should also be valid. The author replied that this is an analogy with a difference. Why? Because the objective and ruling of gift is that the donee becomes its owner, and ownership is established over an undivided share just as over a non-undivided share. The ruling of pawning is different: it is the establishment of the hand of collection, and this ruling cannot be obtained in an undivided share, whether divisible or not. Question: If the matter is that the ruling of gift is establishment of ownership, then gift of a divisible thing should also be valid? Answer: This too is an analogy with a difference, because in a divisible thing, the donor gets caught in the hardship of division, while in a non-divisible thing, that is not the case, so there is no difficulty. Two proofs for the impermissibility of pawning an undivided share. And it is not valid from his co-owner because it does not accept the ruling in the first manner, and in the second manner, he will live one day by virtue of ownership and one day by virtue of pawning, so it becomes as if he pawned it one day and not the other. Translation: And pawning (an undivided share) from his partner is not valid because this undivided share will not accept the ruling of pawning according to the first reason, and according to the second reason, the mortgagee will stay in it one day by virtue of ownership and one day by virtue of pawning, so it becomes as if he kept the pawn one day and not the other. Explanation: Two proofs for the impermissibility of pawning an undivided share were mentioned previously. Non-establishment of the hand of collection and the requirement of continuous confinement. Now listen: If someone pawns a house that is shared between him and Zaid on the basis of common ownership, and he pawns it with Zaid himself, then this is also invalid because according to the first proof, the ruling of pawning is the establishment of the hand of collection, and that is lacking here because the hand of collection is not established over an undivided share. According to the second proof, pawning will also be invalid because continuous confinement is absent; rather, the situation will be that the mortgagee will stay in it one day by virtue of his own ownership and another day by virtue of pawning, meaning it is a pawn one day and not the other, and its impermissibility is clear from what preceded. Therefore, pawning an undivided share from a partner is not valid. Supervening common ownership... statements of jurists. And supervening common ownership prevents the continuation of the pawn in the original narration, and from Abu Yusuf that it does not prevent, because the rule of continuation is easier than the rule of initiation, so it resembles gift.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the impermissibility of pawning an undivided share (musha') in the Hanafi school. It presents two core proofs: (1) the hand of collection (yad al-istifa') cannot be established over a musha' share, and (2) continuous confinement (jabs da'imi) is impossible because the share is jointly owned and must be rotated. The passage then draws a critical distinction between pawning and gift (hibah). While gift of a musha' that is indivisible is valid (since ownership can be established over a share), pawning of any musha'—whether divisible or not—is invalid because the purpose of pawning is not ownership but the right to retain and collect payment, which requires exclusive and continuous possession. The author also addresses an objection: if gift of an indivisible musha' is valid, why not pawning? The answer is that gift's ruling is ownership (which can be in a share), whereas pawning's ruling is the hand of collection (which cannot be in a share). Finally, the passage discusses the case where the musha' is pawned to a co-owner—it is also invalid for the same reasons. At the end, it mentions a subtle intra-Hanafi difference: if common ownership arises after a valid pawn (shuyu' tari'), the original narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) holds that it invalidates the pawn, while Abu Yusuf says it does not, analogizing to gift since continuation is easier than initiation. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the original narration.

Key Terms
شیوع طاری (shuyu' tari'): Common ownership that arises after a valid pawn contract has been concluded, e.g., through inheritance or purchase.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah), what happens to a valid pawn when the mortgagee inherits a share in the pawned property?
A) The pawn remains valid because the mortgagee already had possession.
B) The pawn becomes invalid because the property becomes musha'.
C) The pawn becomes valid only if the inherited share is indivisible.
D) The pawn remains valid if the mortgagee is also the co-owner.

Key Takeaway
Pawning a musha' to a co-owner is invalid, and supervening common ownership invalidates an existing pawn according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Validity of Rahn on Salam Capital, Sarf Price, and Muslam Fih: The Hanafi-Zufar Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on rahn validity for specific debts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of rahn for ra's mal al-salam, thaman al-sarf, and muslam fih, and evaluate Zufar's objection using the concept of maliyyah.

Core Idea
Rahn is valid if homogeneity exists in value, not species — value is the guaranteed aspect.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the validity of rahn for specific debts: the capital in salam, the price in sarf, and the commodity in salam. While Imam Zufar argues that rahn here constitutes prohibited substitution (istibdal) due to lack of species homogeneity, Imam Abu Hanifa and the majority hold that rahn is valid because homogeneity is based on value (maliyyah), and that is what is guaranteed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three items
List the three specific items for which rahn is claimed valid according to the matn: ra's mal al-salam (capital of salam), thaman al-sarf (price in currency exchange), and muslam fih (commodity to be delivered in salam).
These are all forms of debts in specific contracts.
2
State Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that rahn requires istifa' (recovery) of the same species; giving a different item is istibdal (substitution), which is prohibited in sarf and salam.
He considers the lack of species homogeneity fatal.
3
Identify the Hanafi response
The Hanafi position is that homogeneity (mujanasah) is established in terms of value (maliyyah), not physical species.
Value is the common attribute that matters for rahn.
4
Recognize the key concept: madhmun
The guaranteed thing (madhmun) is the value, not the specific item. Therefore, istifa' is realized through the value of the pledge.
This principle is previously established in the text.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: If rahn is given, Zufar would consider it invalid, so the creditor has no security; the Hanafi view allows it, giving the creditor a valid pledge.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويصح الرهن براس مال السلم وبثمن الصرف والمسلم فيه وقال زفر لا يجوز لان حكمه الاستيفاء وهذا استبدال لعدم المجانسة وباب الاستبدال فيها مسدود ولنا ان المجانسة ثابتة في المالية فيتحقق الاستيفاء من حيث المال وهو المضمون على ما مر
He said: The pledge is valid for the capital of salam, the price of sarf, and the muslam fih. Zufar said: It is not permissible because the ruling of rahn is recovery (istifa'), and this is substitution (istibdal) due to lack of homogeneity, and the door of substitution is closed in these matters. Our proof is that homogeneity is established in value (maliyyah), so recovery is realized from the aspect of wealth, which is the guaranteed thing (madhmun) as previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on the validity of rahn for three specific items: the capital (ra's al-mal) in a salam sale, the price (thaman) in a sarf (currency exchange) contract, and the muslam fih (the subject matter of salam). Imam Abu Hanifa (followed by the author) holds that rahn is valid. Imam Zufar objects, arguing that rahn is meant for recovery (istifa') of a debt, but here the debtor is giving something different in kind (istibdal), violating the required homogeneity. The Hanafi response is that homogeneity is based on value (maliyyah), not the specific item. Since both the original obligation and the pledged item share the quality of being valuable wealth, istifa' is achieved through the value. The Urdu commentary elaborates that the pledged item is an amanah (trust), and its value is what is guaranteed, not its physical substance.

Key Terms
راس مال السلم (ra's mal al-salam): The capital (price) paid in a salam sale, which must be received at the time of contract.
ثمن الصرف (thaman al-sarf): The price in a currency exchange (sarf) contract, which must be exchanged hand-to-hand.
مسلم فيه (muslam fih): The commodity to be delivered in a salam sale.
استيفاء (istifa'): Recovery or collection of a debt; the purpose of rahn.
استبدال (istibdal): Substitution of one thing for another; Zufar's objection is that rahn would cause substitution.
مجانسة (mujanasah): Homogeneity in species or type; required for validity of transaction.
مالية (maliyyah): Monetary value; the common attribute that establishes homogeneity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is rahn on the capital of salam (ra's mal al-salam) valid despite Zufar's objection?
A) Because rahn is an amanah, and amanah does not require homogeneity.
B) Because homogeneity exists in terms of value (maliyyah), which is the guaranteed aspect.
C) Because the capital of salam is not a debt, so no homogeneity is needed.
D) Because Zufar's opinion is based on a weak hadith.

Key Takeaway
Rahn on debts in salam and sarf is valid because homogeneity is based on value (maliyyah), not physical species.

Invalidity of Rahn on the Sold Item (Mabee')
Ruling that rahn on the sold item is void

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that rahn on a sold item (mabee') is batil (void) and explain the reason: it is not guaranteed in itself (ghair madhmun bi nafsihi).

Core Idea
Rahn on a sold item is void because the item is not guaranteed in itself.

This short passage from Al-Hidayah declares that taking a pledge (rahn) over a sold item is void. The underlying principle is that a valid rahn requires the pledged property to be a guaranteed liability (madhmun bi nafsihi). In a sale, the seller retains no liability for the item once it is in the buyer's possession; it is held as a trust (amanah). Therefore, a rahn contract on such an item has no legal effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage explicitly states that rahn on the sold item (mabee') is batil (void). Note the legal term used.
2
Understand the reason
The reason given is that the sold item is not guaranteed in itself (ghair madhmun bi nafsihi). That is, the seller does not bear liability for it.
3
Trace the consequence
If the item perishes, the buyer is not liable for compensation because the contract is void. The item remains as a trust (amanah).
4
Relate to the condition for valid rahn
For a rahn contract to be valid, the pledged object must be a guarantee (madhmun). The mabee' fails this condition, making the rahn batil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والرهن بالمبيع باطل لما بينا انه غير مضمون بنفسه فان هلك ذهب بغير شيء لانه لا اعتبار للباطل فبقى قبضا باذنه
He said: The pledge on the sold item is void, because we have clarified that it is not guaranteed in itself. If it perishes, it goes without compensation, for there is no consideration for that which is void; thus it remains as a possession with permission.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This is a short ruling stating that rahn on the sold item (mabee') is invalid (batil). The reason is that the sold item is not a guaranteed thing in itself (ghair madhmun bi nafsihi). This refers to the fact that in a sale, the seller's liability for the item is not a debt; the buyer takes possession with the seller's permission as an amanah. Therefore, if the item is destroyed, the buyer is not liable for compensation. The Urdu commentary explains that since the contract of rahn is invalid, the item remains as a trust (amanah) in the buyer's hands, and no guarantee attaches.

Key Terms
مبیع (mabee'): The item sold in a sale contract, which is in the buyer's possession but not guaranteed.
مضمون بنفسه (madhmun bi nafsihi): Guaranteed in itself; i.e., the owner is liable for its loss or destruction.
باطل (batil): Void or invalid; a contract that has no legal effect from its inception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the sale contract is void.
B) Because the sold item is not guaranteed in itself (ghair madhmun bi nafsihi).
C) Because the buyer does not have possession of the item.
D) Because rahn requires the item to be in debtor's ownership, not buyer's.

Key Takeaway
Rahn on a sold item is batil because the item is not a guarantee (madhmun) – it is merely an amanah in the buyer's hands.
