كتاب الرهن
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۴
باب الرهن الذى يوضع على يد العدل
ترجمہ سید اس رہن کا باب ہے جس کو عادل کے پاس رکھا جاتا ہے
تشریح اب تک تو وہ مسائل مذکور ہوئے جن میں مرہون مرتبن کے پاس رکھا گیا ہے اب وہ مسائل ذکرفرمائیں گے جن میں مرہون عادل کے پاس رہن رکھدیں اور یہ صرف حفاظت کا مامور ہے اس کو یہ حق نہیں ہے راہن اور مرتہن کی جانب سے تسلیط کے بغیر مرہون کو فروخت کر دئے۔
عادل کے پاس رہن رکھنے کا حکم ، اقوال فقہاء
قال واذا اتفقا على وضع الرهن على يد العدل جاز قال مالك لا يجوز ذكر قوله في بعض النسخ لان يد العدل يد المالك ولهذا يرجع العدل عليه عند الاستحقاق فانعدم القبض ولنا ان يده على الصورة يد المالک فی الحفظ اذ العین امانة وفى حق المالية يد المرتهن لان يده يدضمان والمضمون هو المالية فنزل منزلة الشخصين تحقيقا لما قصداه من الرهن وانما يرجع العدل على المالك في الاستحقاق لانه نائب عنه في حفظ العين كالمودع
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب وہ دونوں ( راہن و مرتهن ) عادل کے پاس رہن رکھنے پر اتفاق کرلیں تو جائز ہے مالک نے فرمایا جائز نہیں ہے مالک کا قول بعض نسخوں میں مذکور ہے اس لئے کہ عادل کا قبضہ مالک کا قبضہ ہے اور اسی وجہ سے استحقاق کے وقت عادل را ہن پر رجوع کریگا تو مرتین کا معدوم ہو گیا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ صورت مرمون پر عادل تلبیہ نام کا قبضہ ہے حفاظت کے سلسلہ میں اس لئے کہ عین مرهون امانت ہے اور مالیت کے حق میں مرتہن کا قبضہ قبضہ ضمان ہے اور مالیت ہی مضمون ہوتی ہے تو عادل کو ان کے مقصود رہن کو ثابت کرنے کی وجہ سے دو شخصوں کے درجہ میں اتار لیا گیا اور عادل مالک پر رجوع کرتا ہے استحقاق کے اندر اس لئے کہ عادل مالک کا نائب ہے عین مرہون کی حفاظت کے سلسلہ میں مثل مودع کے۔ تشریح اگر راہن اور مرتہن دونوں نے اتفاق کر لیا کہ رہن عادل کے پاس رکھ دیں تو یہ جائز ہے امام مالک کی جانب یہ قول منسوب
ہے کہ جائز نہیں کیوں؟
انہوں نے کہا ہے رہن کے جواز کیلئے ضروری ہے کہ اس پر مرتبہن کا قبضہ ہو جائے اور یہاں مرتین کا قبضہ نہیں ہوا بلکہ عادل کا قبضہ ہے جو راہن کے قبضہ کا قائم مقام ہے۔
سوال حضرت امام مالک صاحب آپ کے پاس اس کی کیا دلیل ہے کہ عادل کا قبضہ راہن کے قبضہ کا نائب ہے؟ جواب دیکھئے اگر مرہون عادل کے پاس بلاک ہو جائے اور اس کے بعد کسی نے اس مرہون میں اپنا استحقاق ثابت کر کے عادل سے تاوان وصول کر لیا تو عادل اس تاوان کو راہن سے وصول کبر یگا را ہن سے وصول کرنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ وہ قبضہ میں راہن ہی کا وکیل تھا ورنہ اگر مرتہن کے قبضہ کا نائب ہوتا تو وہ تاوان مرتہن سے وصول کرتا بہر حال مرتہن کا قبضہ معدوم ہے اس لئے رہن جائز نہ ہوگا یہ
اس قول کی دلیل ہوئی جو امام مالک کی جانب منسوب کیا گیا ہے۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس طرح امام متقدین اور خدا دونوں کا نائب ہے اور یہ اس لئے ضروری ہے تا کہ رہن کا مقصد پورا ہو جائے تو جب عادل دونوں کا نائب ہوا تو یوں کہا جائیگا کہ مرہون میں دو چیزیں ہیں ایک اسکی ذات اور دوسری اس کی مالیت تو عادل ذات و صورت میں تو راہن کا نائب ہے اور مالیت میں مرتہن کا نائب ہے اور مضمون مالیت ہوا کرتی ہے نہ کہ صورت و عین ۔ خلاصہ کلام جب عادل کے واسطہ سے مرہون پر اس کی مالیت میں مرتین کا قبضہ ثابت ہو گیا تو رہن درست ہو گیا اور امام مالک کا اعتراض غلط ثابت ہوا۔ سوال : تو پھر عادل صورت مذکورہ میں تاوان رہن سے کب وصول کرتا ہے۔ جواب: اس لئے کہ عادل مین کی حفاظت میں راہن کا نائب ہے۔ اور یہ بالکل ایسا ہے کہ زید نے خالد کے پاس اپنی ودیعت رکھ دی تو خالد مودع ہے خالد کے پاس یہ ودیعت ہلاک ہوگئی پھر بکر نے اس ودیعت میں اپنا استحقاق ثابت کر کے خالد سے تاوان لیا تو خالد اس تاوان کو زید سے وصول کر یگا ایسے ہی اس صورت میں ہوا ہے۔ تنبیه - مصنف نے اول کتاب الرہن میں فرمایا ہے کہ امام مالک کے نزدیک نفس عقد سے رہن لازم ہو جاتا ہے تو پھر ان کا قول مذکورہ درست نہیں رہتا کہ مرتہن کا قبضہ معدوم ہے ممکن ہے کہ مالک سے اس میں دو روایتیں ہوں۔
تنبية ... ذكر قوله في بعض النسخ ... الخ اس سے مصنف کی مراد یہ بھی ہو سکتی ہے کہ مختصر القدوری کے بعض نسخوں میں امام مالک کا یہ قول مذکور ہے اور بعض میں نہیں ہے۔ اور یہ بھی ہوسکتا ہے کہ سلف کی بعض کتابوں میں امام مالک کا یہ قول مذکور ہے۔ اور بعض میں امام مالک کے بجائے یہاں ابن ابی لیلی مذکور ہیں۔ مبسوط اور شرح الاقطع میں ابن ابی لیلی ہے۔ مجمع الانہر میں زفر اور ابن ابی لیلیٰ کا یہی قول مذکور ہے۔
Book of Pawn. Chapter on the pawn that is placed with the trustee. Translation: This is the chapter on the pawn that is placed with a just person (trustee). Explanation: Until now, the issues where the pawn is kept with the mortgagor have been mentioned; now issues where the pawn is kept with a trustee will be discussed. He is only appointed for safekeeping and does not have the right to sell the pawn without authorization from the rahin and murtahin. Ruling on placing pawn with a trustee and statements of jurists. Al-Quduri said: And if they both agree to place the pawn with the trustee, it is permissible. Malik said: It is not permissible. His statement is mentioned in some copies because the trustee's possession is the possession of the owner, and for this reason the trustee would recourse to the owner in case of claim, so possession (by the murtahin) is absent. Our proof is that his (the trustee's) possession in form is the possession of the owner in terms of safekeeping because the object is a trust (amanah), and in terms of financial value it is the possession of the murtahin because his hand is a hand of liability, and what is subject to liability is the financial value. So he (the trustee) is placed in the position of two persons to realize what they intended by the pawn. The trustee only recourses to the owner (rahin) in case of claim because he is his deputy in safekeeping of the object, like a depositary. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And when the two (rahin and murtahin) agree to place the pawn with the trustee, it is permissible. Malik said: It is not permissible. Malik's statement is mentioned in some copies because the trustee's possession is the owner's possession, and for this reason the trustee will recourse to the rahin at the time of claim, so the murtahin's possession is absent. Our proof is that in form the trustee's possession is the possession of the owner in terms of safekeeping because the pawned object is a trust, and in terms of financial value it is the possession of the murtahin because his hand is a hand of liability, and what is subject to liability is the financial value. So the trustee is placed in the position of two persons to realize their intended purpose of the pawn. The trustee only recourses to the owner (rahin) in case of claim because he is the owner's deputy in safekeeping of the object, like a depositary. Explanation: If the rahin and murtahin both agree to place the pawn with the trustee, it is permissible. Imam Malik's side has this statement attributed that it is not permissible. Why? They said for the validity of pawn it is necessary that the murtahin take possession, and here the murtahin's possession did not occur; rather the trustee's possession, which stands in place of the rahin's possession. Question: O Imam Malik, what is your proof that the trustee's possession is the deputy of the rahin's possession? Answer: Consider: if the pawn is destroyed while with the trustee, and then someone proves their claim to the pawn and recovers compensation from the trustee, the trustee will recover that compensation from the rahin. Recovering from the rahin is proof that he was the rahin's agent in possession; otherwise, if he were the murtahin's deputy, he would recover from the murtahin. In any case, the murtahin's possession is absent, so the pawn is not valid. This is the proof for the statement attributed to Imam Malik. Our proof is that just as ... the trustee is the deputy of both, and this is necessary so that the purpose of pawn is fulfilled. So when the trustee is the deputy of both, it will be said that the pawn has two aspects: one its physical entity and the other its financial value. The trustee in physical form and aspect is the deputy of the rahin, and in financial value he is the deputy of the murtahin, and what is subject to liability is the financial value, not the form and entity. Summary: When through the trustee the murtahin's possession over the pawn in terms of its financial value is established, the pawn becomes valid, and Imam Malik's objection is proven wrong. Question: Then why does the trustee recover compensation from the rahin in the mentioned case? Answer: Because the trustee in safekeeping of the object is the deputy of the rahin, and this is exactly like when Zaid placed his deposit with Khalid, then Khalid is the depositary. The deposit perished, then Bakr proved his claim to the deposit and took compensation from Khalid; then Khalid recovers that compensation from Zaid. Similarly here. Note: The author earlier in the book of pawn stated that according to Imam Malik the contract alone makes the pawn binding, so then his stated opinion is not consistent that the murtahin's possession is absent. Perhaps Malik has two narrations on this. Note: 'His statement is mentioned in some copies' etc. The author's intent may be that in some copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, Imam Malik's statement is mentioned and in some it is not. Or it may be that in some books of the predecessors, Imam Malik's statement is mentioned, and in some, instead of Imam Malik, Ibn Abi Layla is mentioned. In al-Mabsut and Sharh al-Aqta', it is Ibn Abi Layla. In Majma' al-Anhur, Zufar and Ibn Abi Layla have this same statement.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the validity of placing a pawn (marhun) in the custody of a third-party trustee (al-‘adl). The Hanafi position, stated by al-Quduri, is that this is permissible (ja'iz) if both parties agree. Imam Malik's opposite view, recorded in some textual variants, holds it invalid because the murtahin's possession is absent. The Hanafi proof (dalil) is based on analysing the trustee's possession as dual: in terms of physical safekeeping, it represents the rahin (since the object is an amanah), but in terms of financial liability, it represents the murtahin (since the debt is secured). Thus the trustee stands in the place of both persons, satisfying the requirement of possession for validity. The author rebuts Imam Malik's evidence—that the trustee would recourse to the rahin in case of a third-party claim—by analogising the trustee to a depositary (mudi‘), who similarly recourses to the depositor. A note clarifies that in some sources, Ibn Abi Layla or Zufar replace Imam Malik. The Hanafi view remains the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.

Key Terms
العدل (al-‘adl): A trustworthy third party appointed by both the rahin and murtahin to hold the pawned item for safekeeping.
يد (yad): Possession or custody; in this context, legal control over the pawned item.
ضمان (daman): Liability; the risk of loss that falls on the person holding the item for security.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is placing a pawn with a trustee (al-‘adl) valid despite the murtahin not having direct possession?
A) Because the trustee is considered the agent of the murtahin only, so his possession suffices.
B) Because the trustee's possession is dual: physically for the rahin (amanah) and financially for the murtahin (daman), fulfilling both purposes.
C) Because the contract alone transfers possession to the murtahin, regardless of who holds the item.
D) Because Imam Malik's objection is based on a variant text and is not authoritative.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates pawn with a trustee by treating the trustee as a dual representative: physical custody for the rahin, financial liability for the murtahin.

Neither Party May Take the Pawn from the Trustee
Ruling prohibition on removing pawn from trustee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prohibition on unilateral removal of pawn from the trustee and explain the consequence of its destruction.

Core Idea
Both parties' rights are attached: taking the pawn nullifies the other's right.

Once a pawn is placed with a trustee, neither the rahin (mortgagor) nor the murtahin (mortgagee) may take it back without mutual consent. This protects each party's vested interest: the rahin's right in safe custody and the murtahin's security interest. If the pawn is lost in the trustee's hands, it is treated as lost in the murtahin's guarantee—meaning the debt is reduced or extinguished accordingly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The passage states that neither the rahin nor the murtahin has the right to take the pawn from the trustee. This is a prohibition (haram).
The act is taking the pawn unilaterally from the neutral trustee.
2
Understand the Rationale
The rahin's right is in the safekeeping (the trustee's hand and trust); the murtahin's right is in the financial recovery (istifa'). Allowing one to take would nullify the other's attached right.
The attachment is twofold: physical and financial.
3
Follow the Consequence of Loss
If the pawn is destroyed in the trustee's hand, it is considered lost in the murtahin's liability (daman), meaning the murtahin bears the financial risk and the debt is reduced.
The trustee's possession is deemed as the murtahin's possession for financial purposes.
4
Apply the Principle
This ruling applies as long as the pawn is in the trustee's custody and both parties have not consented to its removal. It underscores the mutual respect of rights in a tripartite rahn contract.
The same logic extends to any third-party custodian appointed by mutual agreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وليس للمرتهن ولا للراهن أن يأخذه منه لتعلق حق الراهن فى الحفظ بيده وامانته وتعلق حق المرتهن به استيفاء فلا يملك احدهما ابطال حق الآخر فلو هلک فی یده هلک فی ضمان المرتهن لان يده في حق المالية المرتهن وهى المضمونة
ترجمہ ... قدوری نے فرمایا اور مرتہن اور راہن کو یہ حق نہیں کہ مرہون کو عادل سے لے لے عادل کے قبضہ اور اس کی امانت کی وجہ سے حفاظت کے سلسلہ میں راہن کا متعلق ہونے کی وجہ سے اور حق مرتہن کے متعلق ہونے کی وجہ سے مرہون کے ساتھ استیفاء کے اعتبار سے تو ان میں سے کوئی ایک دوسرے کا حق باطل کرنے کا مالک نہ ہوگا پس اگر مرہون عادل کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو جائے تو مرتبہن بنی کا قبضہ ہے اور مالیت ہی مضمون ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح وہ مرہون جو عادل کے پاس رکھا گیا ہے چونکہ اس میں راہن اور مرتبہن دونوں کا حق ہے اول کا باعتبار معین اور ثانی کا باعتبار مالیت لہذا عاقدین میں سے کسی کو یہ حق نہ ہوگا کہ دوسرے کا حق باطل کر دے۔ لہذا ان میں سے کسی کو یہ حق بھی نہ ہوگا کہ مرہون کو عادل سے لے لے۔ پھر اگر یہ مرہون عادل کے پاس بلاک ہو جائے تو مرتہن کی ضمانت میں بلاک ہو گا اور حسب تفصیل سابق قرض ساقط ہوگا کیونکہ مرہون پر اعتبار مالیت عادل کا قبضہ مرتہن کے قبضہ کے قائم مقام ہے اور مالیت ہی مضمون ہوا کرتی ہے۔
Al-Quduri said: And neither the murtahin nor the rahin has the right to take it (the pawn) from him (the trustee), because the rahin's right relates to safekeeping through his hand and his trust, and the murtahin's right relates to recovering (the debt) through it. So neither of them has the power to nullify the other's right. If it is destroyed in his (the trustee's) hand, it is destroyed in the murtahin's liability because his (the trustee's) hand in terms of financial value is (that of) the murtahin, and it is the financial value that is subject to liability. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And the murtahin and the rahin do not have the right to take the pawn from the trustee, because the rahin's right is attached to the trustee's hand and his trust in terms of safekeeping, and the murtahin's right is attached to the pawn in terms of recovery (of the debt). So neither of them can nullify the other's right. After that, if the pawn is destroyed in the trustee's hand, it is destroyed in the murtahin's guarantee, as per previous detail; the debt will be extinguished because in terms of financial value, the trustee's possession stands in place of the murtahin's possession, and it is the financial value that is subject to liability. Explanation: Since the pawn placed with the trustee involves rights of both the rahin and the murtahin—the former in terms of the physical object, the latter in terms of financial value—therefore neither party has the right to nullify the other's right. Hence neither has the right to take the pawn from the trustee. Then if the pawn is destroyed while with the trustee, it is destroyed in the murtahin's guarantee, and according to previous detail the debt will be extinguished because in terms of financial value the trustee's possession stands in place of the murtahin's possession, and it is the financial value that is subject to liability.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from al-Quduri that once the pawn is placed in the trustee's custody, neither the mortgagor (rahin) nor the mortgagee (murtahin) has the right to unilaterally take the pawn back from the trustee. The reason is that both have attached rights: the rahin has a right in the physical safekeeping of the object (since he trusts the trustee), and the murtahin has a right to use the pawn as security for his debt. Allowing one party to take the pawn would nullify the other's right. The consequence of loss: if the pawn is destroyed in the trustee's hands, it is considered lost in the murtahin's guarantee (daman), meaning the debt is reduced or extinguished accordingly. This is because the trustee's custody is treated as the murtahin's custody for financial purposes.

Key Terms
استيفاء (istifa'): The murtahin's right to recover his debt from the pawn; i.e., the right to sell the pawn and collect the debt if unpaid.
الراهن (al-rahin): The pawnor, i.e., the person who gives an asset as security for a debt.
المرتهن (al-murtahin): The pawnee, i.e., the creditor who receives the pawn as security for the debt.
العادل (al-'adl): The neutral trustee appointed to hold the pawn, ensuring both parties' rights are protected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the pawned item is destroyed while in the trustee's possession, what is the consequence according to this passage?
A) The rahin bears the loss and still owes the full debt.
B) The trustee is liable to compensate both parties.
C) It is lost in the murtahin's guarantee, and the debt is reduced accordingly.
D) The pawn contract becomes void and both parties revert to pre-contract state.

Key Takeaway
Once a pawn is placed with a trustee, neither party may unilaterally take it; loss in the trustee's hand falls on the murtahin's guarantee.

Trustee's Liability for Handing Pawn to Either Party
Ruling that trustee is liable if he delivers pawn to either party without authorization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a pawn trustee becomes liable if he delivers the pawn to either the rahin or murtahin without the other's consent, and explain the reasoning based on the dual depositary relationship.

Core Idea
Each party is a stranger to the other's deposit; delivering to either one is like delivering to an outsider.

This ruling clarifies a critical aspect of pawn transactions: the trustee (adl) is not simply a custodian for the owner alone. He holds the pawn as a depositary (mudi‘) for both the rahin (pawnor) and the murtahin (pawned), each with a distinct interest. Therefore, handing the pawn to either party without the other's consent violates the trust of the other, triggering liability for the value of the pawn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal consequence
What is the trustee's action? He hands over the pawn to either the rahin or the murtahin. The consequence stated is that he becomes liable (damin).
2
Understand the dual depositary relationship
Why is the trustee liable to both? Because he is a depositary for the rahin regarding the physical object (ayn) and a depositary for the murtahin regarding the financial value (maliyyah).
The murtahin has a security interest in the value.
3
Apply the concept of ajnabi (stranger)
For each deposit, the other party is an outsider (ajnabi). Delivering to an outsider without permission makes a depositary liable. So delivering to the rahin violates the murtahin's deposit, and vice versa.
Hanafi rule: al-mudi‘ yadman bi al-daf‘ ila al-ajnabi (the depositary becomes liable by delivering to a stranger).
4
State the ruling in practical terms
The trustee must obtain consent from both parties before releasing the pawn to either. Without joint consent, any unilateral delivery triggers liability for the full value if the pawn is lost or damaged.
The ruling applies equally to delivery to rahin or murtahin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو دفع العدل الى الراهن او المرتهن ضمن لانه مودع الراهن في حق العين ومودع المرتهن في حق المالية واحدهما اجنب جنبي عن الاخر والمودع يضمن بالدفع الى الاجنبي
And if the trustee hands it over to the rahin or the murtahin, he becomes liable, because he is a depositary for the rahin in respect of the physical object and a depositary for the murtahin in respect of the financial value, and each of them is a stranger (ajnabi) in relation to the other. And the depositary becomes liable when he hands over to a stranger.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This is a ruling statement addressing the liability of the trustee. Since the trustee acts as a depositary (mudi‘) for both parties—for the rahin regarding the physical object, and for the murtahin regarding the financial value—each party is considered a 'stranger' (ajnabi) with respect to the other's depositary role. Therefore, if the trustee hands the pawn to either the rahin or the murtahin without the other's consent, he becomes liable (damān) for its value, just as a depositary becomes liable when he delivers a deposit to a third party without authorization. The practical implication: the trustee must keep the pawn until both parties agree on its disposition.

Key Terms
أجنبي (ajnabi): A person who is a stranger to the depositary relationship; here, each party is a stranger to the other's depositary aspect.
ضمن (damin): He becomes liable (guarantor) for the value of the pawn if it is lost or damaged after his unauthorized delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, when does the trustee become liable for the pawn?
A) If the pawn is lost due to natural disaster while in his custody.
B) If he hands over the pawn to either the rahin or the murtahin without the other's consent.
C) If he refuses to hand over the pawn at the request of the rahin.
D) If he sells the pawn with the permission of both parties.

Key Takeaway
The trustee in a pawn contract is a depositary for both parties; delivering to either rahin or murtahin without the other's consent triggers liability for the pawn's value.

Buyer's Recourse When Sold Pledged Property Is Reclaimed
Stating the ruling for the second scenario where the marhun remains with the buyer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a sold pledged property is reclaimed by its rightful owner while still in the buyer's possession, and identify the party from whom the buyer recovers the price.

Core Idea
The rightful owner takes his property from the buyer; the buyer recovers the price from the 'adl, not the pledgor.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario from the Hidayah on the sale of pledged property. When the property sold by the 'adl turns out to belong to a third party, the rights and liabilities shift depending on whether the property is destroyed or still in hand. Here, the property is still in the buyer's possession, and the text explains the legal recourse for both the rightful owner and the buyer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the sold marhun is still in the buyer's hand (qāʾim fī yad al-mushtarī). This is the second of two scenarios; the first was when it was destroyed.
The scenario assumes the 'adl sold the marhun without authority or the property belonged to a third party.
2
State the ruling for the mustahiq
The rightful owner (mustahiq) has the right to take his property from the buyer because he has found his own property (wajada ʿayna mālihi).
This is based on the principle that one's own property is reclaimable from any possessor.
3
State the ruling for the buyer
The buyer has the right to recover the price (thaman) from the ʿadl (trustee), because the ʿadl is the contracting party (al-ʿāqid). The rights and obligations of the contract attach to him.
The buyer paid the price to secure the property, but the property was not secured for him.
4
Identify the proofs
Two proofs are given: (1) The mustahiq finds his property, so he takes it. (2) The ʿadl is the contractor, so he bears the liability for return of the price.
These are aqli proofs (qiyas).
5
Understand the practical implication
The ʿadl bears the risk of eviction. The buyer's recourse is not against the pledgor (rāhin) or the pledgee (murtahin) but solely against the ʿadl who acted as seller.
This highlights the ʿadl's personal liability in such transactions.

Source Text

بیع مرہون مشتری کے قبضہ میں ہو تو مستحق کو حق ہے کہ وہ مشتری کے قبضہ سے لے لے
وفى الوجه الثاني وهو ان يكون قائما في يد المشترى فللمستحق ان يأخذه من يده لانه وجد عين ماله ثم فلمشترى ان يرجع على العدل بالثمن لانه العاقد فتتعلق به حقوق العقد وهذا من حقوقه حيث وجب بالبيع وانما اداه ليسلم له المبيع ولم يسلم
ترجمہ اور دوسری صورت میں اور وہ یہ ہے کہ مبیع مرہون مشتری کے قبضہ میں موجود ہو تو مستحق کو حق ہے کہ وہ اس کو مشتری کے قبضہ سے لے لے اس لئے کہ اس نے بعینہ اپنے مال کو پا لیا پھر مشتری کو حق ہے کہ وہ عادل سے ثمن واپس لے لے اس لئے کہ عاقد تو عادل ہے تو حقوق عقد اس سے متعلق ہوں گے اور یہ (رجوع شمن ) عقد کے حقوق میں سے ہے کیونکہ ثمن بیچ ہی کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا ہے اور مشتری نے عادل کو اس لئے شمن دیا ہے تاکہ مبیع اس کے لئے سالم رہے حالانکہ وہ سالم نہیں رہی۔ تشریح یہ ساری تفصیلات مذکورہ اس وقت تھیں جب کہ مرہون مشتری کے قبضہ میں ہلاک ہو جائے اور اگر مشتری کے پاس طبیع مرہون موجود ہے تو اس کا حکم اور ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ مستحق کو حق ہے کہ مشتری کے پاس سے اپنا مال لے لے کیونکہ اس نے اپنے مال کو پالیا تو اس کو لینے کا حق ہوگا۔
If the sold pledged property is in the buyer's possession, the rightful owner has the right to take it from the buyer's possession. And in the second way—that it is present in the hand of the buyer—the rightful owner has the right to take it from him because he has found his own property. Then the buyer has the right to resort to the 'adl (trustee) for the price because he is the contracting party; thus the rights of the contract attach to him. And this is among his rights because it became obligatory by the sale, and he only paid it so that the sold item would be safe for him, but it was not safe. Translation: And in the second case, that is, when the sold pledged property is present in the buyer's possession, the rightful owner has the right to take it from the buyer's possession because he has found his own property. Then the buyer has the right to take back the price from the 'adl because the 'adl is the contracting party, so the rights of the contract relate to him. And this (resorting for the price) is among the rights of the contract because the price became obligatory due to the sale, and the buyer paid it to the 'adl so that the sold property would be safe for him, whereas it did not remain safe. Explanation: All these mentioned details were for when the pledged property is destroyed in the buyer's possession. But if the sold pledged property is present with the buyer, then its ruling is different: the rightful owner has the right to take his property from the buyer because he has found his property. So he has the right to take it.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hidayah concerning a scenario where a pledged property (marhun) sold by the 'adl (trustee) turns out to actually belong to a third party (mustahiq). The passage is a 'ruling with proof' type. It addresses the second scenario: the sold property still exists in the buyer's hand. The ruling is that the rightful owner (mustahiq) may reclaim it from the buyer, since he has found his own property. The buyer, in turn, has the right to recover the price (thaman) from the 'adl. The proof given is twofold: (1) the rightful owner found his property, so he takes it; (2) the 'adl is the actual contracting party (al-aqid), so the rights and liabilities of the contract, including the obligation to return the price if the sold item is not delivered, attach to him. The buyer paid the price to secure the property, but it was not secured (since it was taken by the rightful owner). The commentary emphasizes that this differs from the first scenario, where the property was destroyed in the buyer's hand. The key legal principle here is that the 'adl, being the one who acted in the sale, bears the risk of eviction. This is based on the Hanafi position that the selling agent (even if acting for the pledgor/rahin) is personally liable if the buyer does not get the property.

Key Terms
مستحق (mustahiq): The person who rightfully owns the property that was sold as pledged property.
عادل (adl): The trustee appointed to hold the pledged property and authorized to sell it if needed.
ثمن (thaman): The price paid by the buyer for the sold property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a sold pledged property remains in the buyer's possession and is claimed by a rightful owner, from whom does the buyer recover the price?
A) From the rightful owner.
B) From the pledgor (rahin).
C) From the pledgee (murtahin).
D) From the 'adl (trustee).

Key Takeaway
When a sold pledged property is reclaimed by its rightful owner from the buyer, the buyer's recourse is against the 'adl, not the pledgor.
